<dsc reserve="1604" >This model is an XDE model template for the &quot;Overall Design Model&quot;, as describe in the &quot;XDE Model Structure Guidelines&quot;.

The “Overall Design Model” describes the design of the application as a whole and contains elements that span multiple XDE roundtrip models.  It contains the logical partitions that inspire the organization of the individual roundtrip models, as well as the Use-Case Realizations that tie everything together (the Use-Case Realizations describe the collaboration amongst the design elements from the different roundtrip models).  The “Overall Design Model” contains diagrams that refer to the roundtripped design elements.  

Maintaining the “Overall Design Model” is optional, but may be a good idea for organizing diagrams, raising the level of abstraction, etc., as well as providing a place for design elements while still figuring out what implementation mechanism to apply.

This “Design Model” structure contains the following packages:
+ The «layer» packages contain (or contain diagrams that reference) the design elements (Design Classes, Interfaces, and Design Subsystems).  Instances of these design elements appear on the diagrams in the &quot;Use-Case Realization&quot; package.
+ The &quot;Use-Case Realizations package&quot; contains the design-level Use-Case Realizations that describe how the design elements interact to perform the Use Cases.

For more information on these packages, view their model documentation.

The diagrams representing architectural views include “View” in the diagram name.  For more information on these diagrams, view their model documentation.</dsc>
<nam>Main</nam>
<typ>CLASS</typ>

<dsc reserve="1202" >The “Logical View: Key Abstractions” diagram contains the key abstractions of the system.  There are several options for maintaining these key abstractions:

+ A complete Analysis Model is maintained.  In that case, the “Logical View: Key Abstractions” diagram contains the Analysis Classes from the Analysis Model that represent the key abstractions of the system.  

+ A partial Analysis Model is maintained, namely, just the key abstractions.  In that case, the “Logical View: Key Abstractions” diagram contains the Analysis Classes from the Analysis Model that represent the key abstractions of the system.

+ No part of the Analysis Model is maintained.  In that case, the Analysis Classes that represent the key abstractions can be maintained in a package in the Design Model, called “Key Abstractions”

In any case, the &lt;&lt;entity&gt;&gt; key abstraction classes shown in the above diagram should be interpreted to be holding places for the actual key abstractions, whose physical location is determined by the approach taken for maintaining key abstractions.  No matter where key abstractions physically reside, a reference to them should appear on the &quot;Logical View: Key Abstractions&quot; diagram.</dsc>
<nam>Logical View: Key Abstractions</nam>
<typ>CLASS</typ>

<dsc reserve="578" >The “Logical View: Overall Design Model Organization” diagram represents the key partitions of the Design Model. 

In this model template, the first level packages are considered layers, where each layer has a specific responsibility. The second level packages further partition the layer package elements by business functionality.  This structure represents a particular partitioning strategy.  It can be replaced with any number of valid structures that represent other partitioning strategies.

For information on any of these packages, view their model documentation.
</dsc>
<nam>Logical View: Overall Design Model Organization</nam>
<typ>CLASS</typ>
</dgx>

<dsc reserve="395" >The “Use-Case Realizations” package contains the design-level Use-Case Realizations. Each of the Use-Case Realizations is associated with a Use Case in the Use-Case Model and has the same name as that Use Case.

All Use-Case Realizations should have the same structure.  For more information on the structure of a use-case realization, view the model documentation of &quot;Use-Case Realization 1&quot;.</dsc>
<nam>Use-Case Realizations</nam>

<dsc reserve="308" >A class used to model information that has been stored by the system, and the associated behavior. <dsc reserve="468" >An optional single character-set modifier of an external method declaration, which governs the character set used to marshal strings during a call to the external method. The Unicode modifier marshals all strings to Unicode values, the Ansi modifier marshals all strings to ANSI values, and the Auto modifier marshals the strings according to COM+ rules based on the name of the method, or the alias name if specified. If no modifier is specified, the default is Ansi.</dsc>
